   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">Saint Lucia</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Country in the West Indies in the eastern Caribbean Sea
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the country. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Saint Lucia (disambiguation)">Saint Lucia (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div>

class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/uː/: 'oo' in 'goose'">uː</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Saint_Lucia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/dd/En-us-Saint_Lucia.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Saint Lucia.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Sainte-Lucie</i>) is an <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> in the West Indies in the eastern <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> on the boundary with the Atlantic Ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-GovC_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GovC-6">[6]</a></sup> The island was previously called <b>Iyonola</b>, the name given to the island by the native <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">Arawaks</a>, and later <b>Hewanorra</b>, the name given by the native <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Caribs</a>, two separate <a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindian</a> peoples. Part of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, it is located north/northeast of the island of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(Antilles)" title="Saint Vincent (Antilles)">Saint Vincent</a>, northwest of <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> and south of <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>. It covers a land area of 617&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (238 square miles) and reported a population of 165,595 in the 2010 census.<sup id="cite_ref-census_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re,_Saint_Lucia" title="Soufrière, Saint Lucia">Soufrière</a> was colonized by the French and was the original capital of the island. Its capital is <a href="/wiki/Castries" title="Castries">Castries</a>. </p>
      <p>The French were the first Europeans to settle on the island. They signed a treaty with the native <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Island Caribs</a> in 1660. England took control of the island from 1663 to 1667. In ensuing years, it was at war with France fourteen times, and the rule of the island changed frequently (it was ruled seven times each by the French and British). In 1814, the British took definitive control of the island. Because it switched so often between British and French control, Saint Lucia was also known as the "Helen of the West" after the Greek mythological character, <a href="/wiki/Helen_of_Troy" title="Helen of Troy">Helen of Troy</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Representative_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Representative government">Representative government</a> came about in 1840 (universal <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">suffrage</a> was established in 1953). From 1958 to 1962, the island was a member of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a>. On 22 February 1979, Saint Lucia became an independent state and a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GovC_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GovC-6">[6]</a></sup> Saint Lucia is a mixed jurisdiction,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> meaning that it has a legal system based in part on both the <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_common_law" class="mw-redirect" title="English common law">English common law</a>. The Civil Code of St. Lucia of 1867 was based on the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Code_of_Lower_Canada" title="Civil Code of Lower Canada">Quebec Civil Code of 1866</a>, as supplemented by English common law-style legislation. It is also a member of <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">Organisation internationale de la Francophonie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>One of the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a>, <i>Saint Lucia</i> was named after <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucy" title="Saint Lucy">Saint Lucy of Syracuse</a> (AD 283 – 304).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Lucia_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Lucia-10">[10]</a></sup> Saint Lucia and <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> are the only two sovereign nations in the world named after a woman (Ireland is named after the Celtic goddess of fertility <a href="/wiki/%C3%89riu" title="Ériu">Eire</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Saint Lucia is the only sovereign nation named after an actual female historical figure. Legend states that French sailors were <a href="/wiki/Shipwreck" title="Shipwreck">shipwrecked</a> on the island on 13 December, the <a href="/wiki/Feast_day" class="mw-redirect" title="Feast day">feast day</a> of St. Lucy, and therefore named the island in her honour.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarmsenEllisDevaux201414_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarmsenEllisDevaux201414-12">[12]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Saint_Lucia" title="History of Saint Lucia">History of Saint Lucia</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonial_period">Pre-colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The first proven inhabitants were the <a href="/wiki/Taino_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Taino people">Arawaks</a>, though there may have been other native peoples prior to this. The Arawak are believed to have come from northern <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> sometime around <a href="/wiki/AD" class="mw-redirect" title="AD">AD</a> 200–400, as there are numerous <a href="/wiki/Archeology" class="mw-redirect" title="Archeology">archaeological</a> sites on the island where specimens of their well-developed <a href="/wiki/Pottery" title="Pottery">pottery</a> have been found. There is evidence to suggest that the Arawak called the island <i>Iouanalao</i>, meaning 'Land of the Iguanas', due to the island's high number of <a href="/wiki/Iguana" title="Iguana">iguanas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AllAbout_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllAbout-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The more aggressive <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Caribs</a> arrived around AD 800, and seized control from the Arawaks by killing their men and assimilating the women into their own society.<sup id="cite_ref-AllAbout_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllAbout-13">[13]</a></sup> They called the island <i>Hewanarau</i>, and later <i>Hewanorra</i> (Ioüanalao, or "there where iguanas are found").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarmsenEllisDevaux201410_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarmsenEllisDevaux201410-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_European_period">Early European period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early European period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> may have sighted the island during his fourth voyage in 1502, since he made landfall on <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>, yet he does not mention the island in his log. <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_la_Cosa" title="Juan de la Cosa">Juan de la Cosa</a> noted the island on his map of 1500, calling it El Falcon, and another island to the south Las Agujas. A Spanish <a href="/wiki/Cedula" class="mw-redirect" title="Cedula">cédula</a> from 1511 mentions the island within the Spanish domain, and a globe in the Vatican made in 1520, shows the island as Sancta Lucia. </p>
      <p>In the late 1550s, the French <a href="/wiki/Pirate" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirate">pirate</a> <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_le_Clerc" title="François le Clerc">François le Clerc</a> (known as <i>Jambe de Bois</i>, due to his wooden leg) set up a camp on <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_Island_(Saint_Lucia)" title="Pigeon Island (Saint Lucia)">Pigeon Island</a>, from where he attacked passing Spanish ships. In 1605, an English vessel called the <i>Oliphe Blossome</i> was blown off-course on its way to <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, and the 67 colonists started a settlement on Saint Lucia, after initially being welcomed by the Carib chief Anthonie. By 26 September 1605 only 19 survived following continued attacks by the Carib chief Augraumart, so the settlers fled the island.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarmsenEllisDevaux201416–21_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarmsenEllisDevaux201416–21-15">[15]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_Colony">French Colony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: French Colony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/French_West_Indies" title="French West Indies">French West Indies</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1664, Thomas Warner (son of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Warner_(explorer)" title="Thomas Warner (explorer)">Sir Thomas Warner</a>, the governor of <a href="/wiki/St_Kitts" class="mw-redirect" title="St Kitts">St Kitts</a>) claimed Saint Lucia for England. He brought 1,000 men to defend it from the French, but after only two years, only 89 survived with the rest dying mostly due to disease. In 1666, the <a href="/wiki/French_West_India_Company" title="French West India Company">French West India Company</a> resumed control of the island, which in 1674 was made an official French crown colony as a dependency of Martinique.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_and_19th_centuries">18th and 19th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 18th and 19th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Windward_Islands" title="British Windward Islands">British Windward Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Both the British and the French found the island attractive after the slave-based sugar industry developed, and during the 18th century the island changed ownership or was declared neutral territory a dozen times, although the French settlements remained and the island was a de facto French colony well into the eighteenth century. </p>
      <p>In 1722, <a href="/wiki/George_I_of_Great_Britain" title="George I of Great Britain">George I of Great Britain</a> granted both Saint Lucia and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Vincent (island)">Saint Vincent</a> to <a href="/wiki/John_Montagu,_2nd_Duke_of_Montagu" title="John Montagu, 2nd Duke of Montagu">The 2nd Duke of Montagu</a>. He in turn appointed <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Uring" title="Nathaniel Uring">Nathaniel Uring</a>, a merchant sea captain and adventurer, as deputy-governor. Uring went to the islands with a group of seven ships, and established settlement at Petit Carenage. Unable to get enough support from British warships, he and the new colonists were quickly run off by the French.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, Britain occupied Saint Lucia for a year. Britain handed the island back to the French at the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris</a> in 1763. Like the English and Dutch on other islands, the French began to develop the land for the cultivation of sugar cane as a commodity crop on large plantations in 1765. </p>
      <p>The British occupied the island again between 1778 and 1784. </p>
      <p>In January 1791, during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(French_Revolution)" title="National Assembly (French Revolution)">National Assembly</a> sent four <i>commissaires</i> to St Lucia to spread their revolutionary philosophy. By August 1791, slaves began to abandon their estates and Governor de Gimat fled. In December 1792, Lt. <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Raymond_de_Lacrosse" title="Jean-Baptiste Raymond de Lacrosse">Jean-Baptiste Raymond de Lacrosse</a> arrived with revolutionary pamphlets, and the impoverished whites and free people of colour began to arm themselves as <i>patriots</i>. On 1 February 1793, France declared war on England and Holland, and General <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Xavier_de_Ricard" title="Nicolas Xavier de Ricard">Nicolas Xavier de Ricard</a> took over as Governor. The <a href="/wiki/National_Convention" title="National Convention">National Convention</a> abolished enslavement on 4 February 1794, but St. Lucia fell to a British invasion led by Vice Admiral <a href="/wiki/John_Jervis,_1st_Earl_of_St_Vincent" title="John Jervis, 1st Earl of St Vincent">John Jervis</a> on 1 April 1794. <a href="/wiki/Morne_Fortune" title="Morne Fortune">Morne Fortune</a> became <i>Fort Charlotte</i>. Soon, a patriot army of resistance, <i>L'Armee Française dans les Bois</i>, began to fight back. Thus started the <a href="/w/index.php?title=First_Brigand_War&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="First Brigand War (page does not exist)">First Brigand War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarmsenEllisDevaux201460–65_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarmsenEllisDevaux201460–65-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A short time later the British invaded the island as a part of the war with France that had recently broken out. On 21 February 1795 a group of locals under the nominal control of <a href="/wiki/Victor_Hugues" title="Victor Hugues">Victor Hugues</a> defeated a battalion of British troops at Vieux Fort and Rabot. In 1796, <a href="/wiki/Castries" title="Castries">Castries</a> was burned as part of the conflict. <a href="/wiki/John_Moore_(British_Army_officer)" title="John Moore (British Army officer)">General John Moore</a> retook Fort Charlotte in 1796 with the <a href="/wiki/27th_(Inniskilling)_Regiment_of_Foot" title="27th (Inniskilling) Regiment of Foot">27th Inniskilling Fusiliers</a> after two days of bitter fighting. As an honour, the Fusiliers' regimental colour was displayed on the flagstaff of the captured fortress at <a href="/wiki/Morne_Fortune" title="Morne Fortune">Morne Fortune</a> for an hour before being replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Union_Jack" title="Union Jack">Union Jack</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Moore would then participate in British efforts to repress the slave rebels until falling ill of <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">yellow fever</a>, upon which he returned to Britain before 1798. </p>
      <p>In 1803, the British regained control of the island. Many of the rebels escaped into the thick rainforest where they evaded capture and established <a href="/wiki/Maroon_communities" class="mw-redirect" title="Maroon communities">maroon communities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The slavery on the island was continued for a short time, but anti-slavery sentiment was rising in Britain. The British stopped the import of slaves by anyone, white or coloured, when they <a href="/wiki/Slave_Trade_Act_1807" title="Slave Trade Act 1807">abolished the slave trade</a> in 1807. </p>
      <p>France and Great Britain continued to contest Saint Lucia until the British secured it in 1814, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1814)" title="Treaty of Paris (1814)">Treaty of Paris</a> ending the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>. Thereafter, Saint Lucia was considered part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Windward_Islands" title="British Windward Islands">British Windward Islands</a> colony. </p>
      <p>The institution of slavery was abolished on the island in 1836, as it was <a href="/wiki/Slavery_Abolition_Act_1833" title="Slavery Abolition Act 1833">throughout the British Empire</a>. After abolition, all former slaves had to serve a four-year "apprenticeship," to accustom them to the idea of freedom. During this period, they worked for their former masters for at least three-quarters of the work week. Full freedom was duly granted by the British in 1838. By that time, people of African ethnicity greatly outnumbered those of ethnic European background. Some people of Carib descent also comprised a minority on the island. </p>
      <p>Castries' harbour was protected by a system of 60 surrounding forts. Along the top of Morne Fortune there are six military sites, building work by the French started in 1768, and the British completed the work by 1890. They include Fort Charlotte (Old Morne Fortress), the Apostle's Battery (1888–1890), The Powder Magazine built by the French in the 1750s, Provost's <a href="/wiki/Redoubt" title="Redoubt">Redoubt</a> (1792) built as a lookout point, and the Combermere <a href="/wiki/Barracks" title="Barracks">barracks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Saint_Lucia_(1939%E2%80%931967).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Flag_of_Saint_Lucia_%281939%E2%80%931967%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Saint_Lucia_%281939%E2%80%931967%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Flag_of_Saint_Lucia_%281939%E2%80%931967%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Saint_Lucia_%281939%E2%80%931967%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Flag_of_Saint_Lucia_%281939%E2%80%931967%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Saint_Lucia_%281939%E2%80%931967%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Saint_Lucia_(1939%E2%80%931967).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Flag of Saint Lucia">Flag of Saint Lucia</a> 1939–1967
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The best preserved installation is a battery at La Toc Point, completed in 1888 it was not abandoned till 1905. This fort in particular was built by the British to repel any attack from the United States on the then valuable <a href="/wiki/Coaling_(ships)" title="Coaling (ships)">coaling harbour</a> of Castries.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> visited the island directly during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Caribbean" title="Battle of the Caribbean">Battle of the Caribbean</a>, when a German <a href="/wiki/U-boat" title="U-boat">U-boat</a> attacked and sank two British ships in <a href="/wiki/Castries" title="Castries">Castries</a> harbour on 9 March 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarmsenEllisDevaux2014275_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarmsenEllisDevaux2014275-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the mid-twentieth century, Saint Lucia joined the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> (1958–1962) when the colony was dissolved. In 1967, Saint Lucia became one of the six members of the West Indies Associated States, with internal self-government. In 1979, it gained full independence under <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_Compton" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir John Compton">Sir John Compton</a> of the conservative <a href="/wiki/United_Workers_Party_(Saint_Lucia)" title="United Workers Party (Saint Lucia)">United Workers party (UWP)</a>. The new country chose to remain within the <a href="/wiki/British_Commonwealth" class="mw-redirect" title="British Commonwealth">British Commonwealth</a> and to retain Queen Elizabeth as <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Monarchy of Saint Lucia">Monarch</a>, represented locally by a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Governor-General of Saint Lucia">Governor-General</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-independence_era">Post-independence era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Post-independence era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Compton's initial term as Prime Minister lasted only a few months, as he was defeated by the left-leaning <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia_Labour_Party" title="Saint Lucia Labour Party">Saint Lucia Labour Party</a> (SLP) under <a href="/wiki/Allan_Louisy" title="Allan Louisy">Allan Louisy</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1979_Saint_Lucian_general_election" title="1979 Saint Lucian general election">1979 Saint Lucian general election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-24">[24]</a></sup> The SLP sought to improve ties with socialist countries in the region such as <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, though the economy was severely affected by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Allen" title="Hurricane Allen">Hurricane Allen</a> in 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_–_St_Lucia_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_–_St_Lucia-25">[25]</a></sup> Louisy was replaced as Prime Minister by <a href="/wiki/Winston_Cenac" title="Winston Cenac">Winston Cenac</a> in 1981. The SLP government faced a series of strikes and Cenac agreed to stand down, with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Pilgrim" title="Michael Pilgrim">Michael Pilgrim</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Labour_Party_(Saint_Lucia)" title="Progressive Labour Party (Saint Lucia)">Progressive Labour Party</a> briefly serving as Acting Prime Minister until the <a href="/wiki/1982_Saint_Lucian_general_election" title="1982 Saint Lucian general election">1982 Saint Lucian general election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> This election was won by the UWP under John Compton, who proceeded to rule the country uninterrupted until 1996;<sup id="cite_ref-john_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-john-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-compton_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-compton-28">[28]</a></sup> he was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Vaughan_Lewis" title="Vaughan Lewis">Vaughan Lewis</a>, who ruled for just over a year before losing the <a href="/wiki/1997_Saint_Lucian_general_election" title="1997 Saint Lucian general election">1997 Saint Lucian general election</a> to the SLP under <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Anthony" title="Kenny Anthony">Kenny Anthony</a>. During this era the UWP adopted a generally pro-Western, pro-business outlook, seeking to diversify the economy away from over-reliance on bananas and boosting the tourism sector.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_–_St_Lucia_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_–_St_Lucia-25">[25]</a></sup> Compton was also a keen advocate of regional integration.<sup id="cite_ref-compton_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-compton-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Anthony remained in power until 2006 when the UWP, again led by Compton, <a href="/wiki/2006_Saint_Lucian_general_election" title="2006 Saint Lucian general election">won control</a> of parliament. Compton pledged to boost the economy and tackle the rising crime rate.<sup id="cite_ref-claims_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-claims-29">[29]</a></sup> Police attempts to curb crime were criticised in 2015 when it emerged that several suspects had been unlawfully shot by police and the circumstances of their deaths covered up.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_–_St_Lucia_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_–_St_Lucia-25">[25]</a></sup> In May 2007, after Compton suffered a series of small strokes,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Finance and External Affairs Minister <a href="/wiki/Stephenson_King" title="Stephenson King">Stephenson King</a> became acting prime minister and succeeded Compton as Prime Minister when the latter died in September 2007. In November 2011, Kenny Anthony was <a href="/wiki/2011_Saint_Lucian_general_election" title="2011 Saint Lucian general election">re-elected</a> as prime minister for a third time.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2016_Saint_Lucian_general_election" title="2016 Saint Lucian general election">June 2016 election</a> the United Worker's Party (UWP) assumed power again, with <a href="/wiki/Allen_Chastanet" title="Allen Chastanet">Allen Chastanet</a> becoming prime minister.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Geography of Saint Lucia">Geography of Saint Lucia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Lucia_geography_map_en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Saint_Lucia_geography_map_en.png/200px-Saint_Lucia_geography_map_en.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="283" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Saint_Lucia_geography_map_en.png/300px-Saint_Lucia_geography_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Saint_Lucia_geography_map_en.png/400px-Saint_Lucia_geography_map_en.png 2x" data-file-width="733" data-file-height="1036"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Lucia_geography_map_en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of Saint Lucia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanic</a> island of Saint Lucia is more mountainous than most <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> islands, with the highest point being <a href="/wiki/Mount_Gimie" title="Mount Gimie">Mount Gimie</a>, at 950 metres (3,120 feet) above <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Lucia_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Lucia-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_–_St_Lucia_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_–_St_Lucia-25">[25]</a></sup> Two other mountains, the <a href="/wiki/Pitons" title="Pitons">Pitons</a>, form the island's most famous landmark.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Lucia_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Lucia-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_–_St_Lucia_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_–_St_Lucia-25">[25]</a></sup> They are located between <a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re,_Saint_Lucia" title="Soufrière, Saint Lucia">Soufrière</a> and <a href="/wiki/Choiseul,_Saint_Lucia" title="Choiseul, Saint Lucia">Choiseul</a> on the western side of the island. Saint Lucia is the only island in the world that contains a drive-in volcano.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (December 2019)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:Saint_Lucia#Dubious" title="Talk:Saint Lucia">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> Forests cover about 77% of the land area.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Lucia_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Lucia-10">[10]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are a number of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Caribbean_islands#Saint_Lucia" title="List of Caribbean islands">small islands</a> off the coast, the largest of which are the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Islands,_St_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Maria Islands, St Lucia (page does not exist)">Maria Islands</a> in the south-east. </p>
      <p>The capital city of Saint Lucia is <a href="/wiki/Castries" title="Castries">Castries</a> (population 60,263) where 32.4% of the population lives. Other major towns include <a href="/wiki/Gros_Islet" title="Gros Islet">Gros Islet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re,_Saint_Lucia" title="Soufrière, Saint Lucia">Soufrière</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vieux_Fort" class="mw-redirect" title="Vieux Fort">Vieux Fort</a>. The population tends to be concentrated around the coast, with the interior more sparsely populated, due to the presence of dense forests.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Lucia_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Lucia-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_–_St_Lucia_25-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_–_St_Lucia-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The local climate is <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical</a>, specifically a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">tropical rainforest climate</a> (Af) under the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>, moderated by northeast <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a>, with a dry season from 1 December to 31 May, and a wet season from 1 June to 30 November (referred to by locals as the hurricane season). </p>
      <p>Average daytime temperatures are around 30&nbsp;°C (86.0&nbsp;°F), and average nighttime temperatures are around 24&nbsp;°C (75.2&nbsp;°F). Since it is fairly close to the equator, the temperature does not fluctuate much between winter and summer. Average annual rainfall ranges from 1,300&nbsp;mm (51.2&nbsp;in) on the coast to 3,810&nbsp;mm (150&nbsp;in) in the mountain rainforests. </p>

      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Saint Lucia contains five terrestrial ecoregions: Windward Islands moist forests, Leeward Islands dry forests, Windward Islands dry forests, Windward Islands xeric scrub, and <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles_mangroves" title="Lesser Antilles mangroves">Lesser Antilles mangroves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-35">[35]</a></sup> It had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 6.17/10, ranking it 84th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A species of lizard, <i><a href="/wiki/Anolis_luciae" title="Anolis luciae">Anolis luciae</a></i>, is named for and is <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> to Saint Lucia.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:USGS_Saint_Lucia_geologic_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/USGS_Saint_Lucia_geologic_map.png/220px-USGS_Saint_Lucia_geologic_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="99" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/USGS_Saint_Lucia_geologic_map.png/330px-USGS_Saint_Lucia_geologic_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/USGS_Saint_Lucia_geologic_map.png/440px-USGS_Saint_Lucia_geologic_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1312" data-file-height="590"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:USGS_Saint_Lucia_geologic_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Saint Lucia <a href="/wiki/Geologic_map" title="Geologic map">geologic map</a>, where Tmov denotes <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene</a>/<a href="/wiki/Oligocene" title="Oligocene">Oligocene</a> volcanic rocks, Tplv are <a href="/wiki/Pliocene" title="Pliocene">Pliocene</a> <a href="/wiki/Calc-alkaline_magma_series" title="Calc-alkaline magma series">calc-alkaline volcanic rocks</a>, and Qv are <a href="/wiki/Quaternary" title="Quaternary">Quaternary</a> volcanic edifices, flows, and pyroclastic deposits.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Qualibou_Caldera_tomography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Qualibou_Caldera_tomography.png/220px-Qualibou_Caldera_tomography.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Qualibou_Caldera_tomography.png/330px-Qualibou_Caldera_tomography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Qualibou_Caldera_tomography.png/440px-Qualibou_Caldera_tomography.png 2x" data-file-width="814" data-file-height="583"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Qualibou_Caldera_tomography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Topography of the Soufriere Volcanic Complex
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The geology of St. Lucia can be described as composing three main areas. The oldest, 16–18 <a href="/wiki/Megaannum" class="mw-redirect" title="Megaannum">Ma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volcanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic">volcanic</a> rocks are exposed from Castries northward and consist of <a href="/wiki/Eroded" class="mw-redirect" title="Eroded">eroded</a> <a href="/wiki/Basalt" title="Basalt">basalt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andesite" title="Andesite">andesite</a> centres. The middle, central highlands, portion of the island consists of dissected andesite centres, 10.4 to 1 Mya, while the lower southwest portion of the island contains recent activity from the Soufriere Volcanic Centre (SVC). This SVC, centred about the <a href="/wiki/Qualibou" title="Qualibou">Qualibou</a> <a href="/wiki/Caldera" title="Caldera">depression</a>, contains <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_flow" title="Pyroclastic flow">pyroclastic flow</a> deposits, <a href="/wiki/Lava_flow" class="mw-redirect" title="Lava flow">lava flows</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intrusive_rock" title="Intrusive rock">domes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Block_and_ash_flow" title="Block and ash flow">block and ash flow</a> deposits, and <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_crater" title="Volcanic crater">explosion craters</a>. This depression's perimeter includes the town of Soufriere, Mount Tabac, Mt. Gimie, Morne Bonin, and Gros Piton. At 10 kilometres (6.2&nbsp;mi) in diameter, though the western portion is open towards the Grenada <a href="/wiki/Basin_(geology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Basin (geology)">basin</a>, the depression formed as recently as 100 kya. The depression is noted for its <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_gradient" title="Geothermal gradient">geothermal activity</a>, especially at <a href="/wiki/Sulphur_Springs,_Saint_Lucia" title="Sulphur Springs, Saint Lucia">Sulphur Springs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re_Estate" title="Soufrière Estate">Soufrière Estates</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Phreatic_eruption" title="Phreatic eruption">phreatic eruption</a> in 1776, and recent <a href="/wiki/Seismic_activity" class="mw-redirect" title="Seismic activity">seismic activity</a> (2000–2001).<sup id="cite_ref-Lindsay_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lindsay-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Eroded andesitic <a href="/wiki/Stratovolcano" title="Stratovolcano">stratovolcanoes</a> to the north east of the depression include <a href="/wiki/Mount_Gimie" title="Mount Gimie">Mt. Gimie</a>, Piton St Esprit, and Mt. Grand Magazin, all greater than 1 Ma in age. Andesitic and <a href="/wiki/Dacite" title="Dacite">dacite</a> pyroclastic flows from these volcanoes are found at Morne Tabac dome (532 <a href="/wiki/Kiloannus" class="mw-redirect" title="Kiloannus">ka</a>), Morne Bonin dome (273 kya), and Bellevue (264 kya). <a href="/wiki/Avalanche" title="Avalanche">Avalanche</a> deposits from the formation of the Qualibou depression are found offshore, and in the massive blocks of Rabot, Pleisance, and Coubaril. The dacitic domes of <a href="/wiki/Petit_Piton" class="mw-redirect" title="Petit Piton">Petit Piton</a> (109 kya) and <a href="/wiki/Gros_Piton" class="mw-redirect" title="Gros Piton">Gros Piton</a> (71 kya) were then <a href="/wiki/Extrusive_rock" title="Extrusive rock">extruded</a> onto the depression floor accompanied by the Anse John (104 kya) and La Pointe (59.8 kya) pyroclastic flows. Later, pyroclastic flows include <a href="/wiki/Pumice" title="Pumice">pumice</a>-rich Belfond and Anse Noir (20 kya). Finally, the dacitic domes of Terre Blanche (15.3 kya) and Belfond (13.6 kya) formed within the depression.<sup id="cite_ref-Lindsay_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lindsay-39">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Politics of Saint Lucia">Politics of Saint Lucia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Saint Lucia is a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a>. <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> is <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Monarchy of Saint Lucia">Queen of Saint Lucia</a>, represented on the island by a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Governor-General of Saint Lucia">governor-general</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Saint_Lucia" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of Saint Lucia">prime minister</a><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> is normally the head of the party commanding the support of the majority of the members of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_Saint_Lucia" title="House of Assembly of Saint Lucia">House of Assembly</a>, which has 17 seats.<sup id="cite_ref-GovHA_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GovHA-41">[41]</a></sup> The other chamber of <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Parliament of Saint Lucia">Parliament</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Senate of Saint Lucia">Senate</a>, has eleven appointed members. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Allen_Chastanet_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Allen_Chastanet_2016.jpg/170px-Allen_Chastanet_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Allen_Chastanet_2016.jpg/255px-Allen_Chastanet_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Allen_Chastanet_2016.jpg/340px-Allen_Chastanet_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="771" data-file-height="998"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Allen_Chastanet_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Allen_Chastanet" title="Allen Chastanet">Allen Chastanet</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Saint Lucia is a two-party parliamentary democracy. Three political parties participated in the 6 June 2016 General Election. The <a href="/wiki/United_Workers_Party_(Saint_Lucia)" title="United Workers Party (Saint Lucia)">United Workers Party</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Allen_Chastanet" title="Allen Chastanet">Allen Chastanet</a>, won eleven of the seventeen seats.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Foreign relations of Saint Lucia">Foreign relations of Saint Lucia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Saint Lucia maintains friendly relations with the major powers active in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. Saint Lucia has no current international disputes. </p>
      <p>Saint Lucia is a full and participating member of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community (CARICOM)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" title="Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States">Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States</a> (OECS), and <a href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="La Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>. Saint Lucia is a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Realm" class="mw-redirect" title="Commonwealth Realm">Commonwealth Realm</a>. </p>
      <p>Saint Lucia became the 152nd member of the United Nations on 9 December 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> As of January 2018, Cosmos Richardson, who presented his credentials on 22 February 2017, was Saint Lucia's representative to the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Organisation_of_American_States_.28OAS.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation_of_American_States_(OAS)">Organisation of American States (OAS)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Organisation of American States (OAS)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Charter of the OAS was signed in Bogota in 1948 and was amended by several protocols which were named after the city and the year in which the protocol was signed, such as Managua in 1993 forming part of the name of the protocol.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Saint Lucia entered the OAS system on 22 February 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agreements_which_impact_on_financial_relationships">Agreements which impact on financial relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Agreements which impact on financial relationships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span id="The_Double_Taxation_Relief_.28CARICOM.29_Treaty_1994"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Double_Taxation_Relief_(CARICOM)_Treaty_1994">The Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty 1994</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: The Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty 1994">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>At a CARICOM Meeting, the representative of St. Lucia, John Compton signed The Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty 1994 on 6 July 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-caricom_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caricom-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The representatives of seven CARICOM countries signed similar agreements at Sherbourne Conference Centre, St. Michael, Barbados.<sup id="cite_ref-caricom_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caricom-47">[47]</a></sup> The countries whose representatives signed the treaties in Barbados were Antigua and Barbuda, Belize, Grenada, Jamaica, St. Kitts and Nevis, St. Vincent and the Grenadines, and Trinidad and Tobago.<sup id="cite_ref-caricom_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caricom-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>This treaty covered taxes, residence, tax jurisdictions, capital gains, business profits, interest, dividends, royalties and other areas. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="FATCA">FATCA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: FATCA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>On 30 June 2014, Saint Lucia signed a Model 1 agreement with the United States of America in relation to <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Account_Tax_Compliance_Act" title="Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act">Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act</a> (FATCA).<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> As of 1 September 2016, the status of the agreement is listed as "in force". </p>
      <p>Preceding the 2014 FATCA agreement is one which was entered into on 30 January 1987 between the United States of America and Saint Lucia according to Paragraph 2 of the Model 1 agreement, the purpose of which was to exchange tax Information.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Military of Saint Lucia">Military of Saint Lucia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Saint Lucia has a paramilitary force. A Special Service Unit (SSU) and the Coast Guard are both under the command of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Saint_Lucia_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Saint Lucia Police">Royal Saint Lucia Police</a>. Although the SSU is under the RSLPF (Royal Saint Lucia Police Force), they are called in as the last line of defence or for more severe cases.<sup id="cite_ref-a_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, Saint Lucia signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Quarters_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Quarters of Saint Lucia">Quarters of Saint Lucia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The districts of the island, established by the French colonial government and continued by the British, are: </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style>
      <div class="div-col"> 
       <ul>
        <li><a href="/wiki/Anse_la_Raye_Quarter" title="Anse la Raye Quarter">Anse la Raye</a>, 31.0&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Canaries_Quarter" class="mw-redirect" title="Canaries Quarter">Canaries</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Castries_Quarter" title="Castries Quarter">Castries</a>, 79.5&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Choiseul_Quarter" title="Choiseul Quarter">Choiseul</a>, 31.3&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Dennery_Quarter" title="Dennery Quarter">Dennery</a>, 69.7&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Gros_Islet_Quarter" title="Gros Islet Quarter">Gros Islet</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Laborie_Quarter" title="Laborie Quarter">Laborie</a>, 37.8&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Micoud_Quarter" title="Micoud Quarter">Micoud</a>, 77.7&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re_Quarter" title="Soufrière Quarter">Soufrière</a>, 50.5&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Vieux_Fort_Quarter" title="Vieux Fort Quarter">Vieux Fort</a>, 43.8&nbsp;km</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <p>An additional area is the Forest Reserve Area Quarter (78.3&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>). </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Economy of Saint Lucia">Economy of Saint Lucia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Lucia_electricity_production.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Saint_Lucia_electricity_production.svg/220px-Saint_Lucia_electricity_production.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Saint_Lucia_electricity_production.svg/330px-Saint_Lucia_electricity_production.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Saint_Lucia_electricity_production.svg/440px-Saint_Lucia_electricity_production.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="639" data-file-height="545"></a>

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> categorizes Saint Lucia as a <a href="/wiki/Small_Island_Developing_States" title="Small Island Developing States">Small Island Developing State</a>, a designation similar to a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a> with a few substantial differences due to Saint Lucia's island nature.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">services sector</a> accounted for 82.8% of GDP, followed by <a href="/wiki/Industrial_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrial sector">industry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> at 14.2% and 2.9%, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-CIAStLucia_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAStLucia-2">[2]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>An educated workforce and improvements in roads, communications, water supply, sewerage, and port facilities have attracted foreign investment in tourism and in petroleum storage and transshipment. However, with the US, Canada, and Europe in recession, tourism declined by double digits in early 2009. The recent change in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> import preference regime and the increased competition from Latin American bananas have made economic diversification increasingly important in Saint Lucia. </p>
      <p>Saint Lucia has been able to attract foreign business and investment, especially in its offshore banking and tourism industries, which is Saint Lucia's main source of revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The manufacturing sector is the most diverse in the Eastern Caribbean area, and the government is trying to revitalise the banana industry. Despite negative growth in 2011, economic fundamentals remain solid, and GDP growth should recover in the future. </p>
      <p>Inflation has been relatively low, averaging 5.5 percent between 2006 and 2008. Saint Lucia's currency is the <a href="/wiki/East_Caribbean_Dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="East Caribbean Dollar">East Caribbean Dollar</a> (EC$), a regional currency shared among members of the Eastern Caribbean Currency Union (ECU). The <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Caribbean_Central_Bank" title="Eastern Caribbean Central Bank">Eastern Caribbean Central Bank</a> (ECCL) issues the EC$, manages monetary policy, and regulates and supervises commercial banking activities in member countries. In 2003, the government began a comprehensive restructuring of the economy, including elimination of price controls and privatization of the state banana company.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Saint_Lucia" title="Tourism in Saint Lucia">Tourism in Saint Lucia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:At_the_top_of_Pigeon_Island.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/At_the_top_of_Pigeon_Island.jpg/220px-At_the_top_of_Pigeon_Island.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/At_the_top_of_Pigeon_Island.jpg/330px-At_the_top_of_Pigeon_Island.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/At_the_top_of_Pigeon_Island.jpg/440px-At_the_top_of_Pigeon_Island.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:At_the_top_of_Pigeon_Island.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Gros Islet and Rodney Bay as seen from Pigeon Island
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Tourism is vital to Saint Lucia's economy. Its economic importance is expected to continue to increase as the market for bananas have become more competitive. Tourism tends to be more substantial during the dry season (January to April), often referred to as the tourist season. Saint Lucia tends to be popular due to its tropical weather and scenery and its beaches and resorts. </p>
      <p>Other tourist attractions include a drive-in <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sulphur_Springs,_Saint_Lucia" title="Sulphur Springs, Saint Lucia">Sulphur Springs</a> (in Soufrière), zip lining in at Sault Falls, Dennery, the <a href="/wiki/St_Lucia_Botanical_Gardens" class="mw-redirect" title="St Lucia Botanical Gardens">Botanical Gardens</a>, the Majestic twin Peaks "The Pitons", a world heritage site, the rain forests, several options of boat trips, Frigate Island Nature Reserve (Operated by the St. Lucia National Trust), Dennery, and Pigeon Island National Park, which is home to Fort Rodney, an old British military base. </p>
      <p>The majority of tourists visit Saint Lucia as part of a cruise. Most of their time tends to be spent in <a href="/wiki/Castries" title="Castries">Castries</a>, although <a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re,_Saint_Lucia" title="Soufrière, Saint Lucia">Soufriere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marigot_Bay" title="Marigot Bay">Marigot Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rodney_Bay" title="Rodney Bay">Rodney Bay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gros_Islet" title="Gros Islet">Gros Islet</a> are also tourist destinations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The current Minister of Tourism is <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Fedee" title="Dominic Fedee">Dominic Fedee</a>, he has been in his role since 2016. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Demographics of Saint Lucia">Demographics of Saint Lucia</a>
      </div>

       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Saint Lucia reported a population of 165,595 in the 2010 national census.<sup id="cite_ref-census_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-7">[7]</a></sup> In 2018, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Population_Division" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Population Division">United Nations Population Division</a> estimated Saint Lucia's population at 181,889.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-59">[59]</a></sup> The country's population is evenly divided between urban and rural areas, with more than a third living in the capital, Castries. </p>
      <p>Despite a high emigration rate, the population is growing rapidly at about 1.2% per year. Migration from Saint Lucia is primarily to <a href="/wiki/English-speaking_world" title="English-speaking world">Anglophone</a> countries, with the United Kingdom having almost 10,000 Saint Lucian-born citizens, and over 30,000 of Saint Lucian heritage. The second most popular destination for Saint Lucian émigrés is the United States, where a combined (foreign and national-born Saint Lucians) almost 14,000 reside. Canada is home to a few thousand Saint Lucians.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Saint Lucia's population is predominantly of African and mixed African-European-Carib descent, with a small <a href="/wiki/Indo-Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-Caribbean">Indo-Caribbean</a> minority (3%). Members of other or unspecified ethnic groups, account for about 2% of the population. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The official language is English.<sup id="cite_ref-sltb-about_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sltb-about-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-usstate-bgnote_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usstate-bgnote-61">[61]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucian_French_Creole" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Lucian French Creole">Saint Lucian French Creole</a> (Kwéyòl), which is colloquially referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Patois" title="Patois">Patois</a></i> ("Patwa"), is spoken by 95% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-creole_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-creole-62">[62]</a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/Antillean_Creole" title="Antillean Creole">Antillean Creole</a> is used in literature and music, and is gaining official acknowledgement.<sup id="cite_ref-creole_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-creole-62">[62]</a></sup> As it developed during the early period of French colonisation, the creole is derived chiefly from French and West African languages, with some vocabulary from the <a href="/wiki/Island_Carib_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Carib language">Island Carib language</a> and other sources. Antillean Creole is also spoken in Dominica, Martinique, Guadeloupe, and (to a lesser extent) St. Vincent and Grenada; it also resembles the creoles spoken in French Guiana, Haiti, Mauritius and the Seychelles. Saint Lucia is a member of <i><a href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="La Francophonie">La Francophonie</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">

         </div>

         <div class="legend">

         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:grey; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Unspecified (1.4%)
         </div>

         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is the main religion in Saint Lucia. About 61.5% of the population is <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>. Another 25.5% belong to Protestant denominations, (includes Seventh Day Adventist 10.4%, Pentecostal 8.9%, Baptist 2.2%, Anglican 1.6%, Church of God 1.5%, other Protestant 0.9%). <a href="/wiki/Evangelicals" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelicals">Evangelicals</a> comprise 2.3% of the population and 1.1% are <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>. In addition, about 1.9% of the population adheres to the <a href="/wiki/Rastafari_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Rastafari movement">Rastafari movement</a>. Other religions include Hinduism, Bahá'í Faith, Judaism, and Buddhism. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><i>See <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Saint_Lucia" title="Health in Saint Lucia">Health in Saint Lucia</a></i> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Saint_Lucia" title="Crime in Saint Lucia">Crime in Saint Lucia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2017, Saint Lucia recorded 60 homicides, the highest in the country's history.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
