      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Culture of Saint Lucia">Culture of Saint Lucia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Day250castriesreduxd.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Day250castriesreduxd.jpg/300px-Day250castriesreduxd.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Day250castriesreduxd.jpg/450px-Day250castriesreduxd.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Day250castriesreduxd.jpg/600px-Day250castriesreduxd.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1474" data-file-height="801"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Day250castriesreduxd.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia_Jazz_Festival" title="Saint Lucia Jazz Festival">Saint Lucia Jazz Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Castries" title="Castries">Castries</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The culture of Saint Lucia has been influenced by African, East Indian, French, and English heritage. One of the secondary languages is <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucian_French_Creole" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Lucian French Creole">Saint Lucian French Creole or Kwéyòl</a>, spoken by almost all of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-sltb-about_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sltb-about-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-usstate-bgnote_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usstate-bgnote-61">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Saint Lucia boasts the highest ratio of <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel</a> laureates produced with respect to the total population of any sovereign country in the world. Two winners have come from Saint Lucia: <a href="/wiki/William_Arthur_Lewis_(economist)" class="mw-redirect" title="William Arthur Lewis (economist)">Sir Arthur Lewis</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Sweden_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences_in_Memory_of_Alfred_Nobel" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of Sweden Prize in Economic Sciences in Memory of Alfred Nobel">Nobel Prize in Economics</a> in 1979, and the poet <a href="/wiki/Derek_Walcott" title="Derek Walcott">Derek Walcott</a> received the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> in 1992. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Saint Lucian cultural festivals include <a href="/wiki/La_Woz" title="La Woz">La Rose</a> celebrated on August 30 and <a href="/wiki/La_Magwit" title="La Magwit">La Marguerite</a> on October 17th, the first representing a native Saint Lucian fraternal society known as the Order of the Rose that is fashioned in the mould of <a href="/wiki/Rosicrucianism" title="Rosicrucianism">Rosicrucianism</a>, and the second representing its traditional rival, the native Saint Lucian equivalent of <a href="/wiki/Freemasonry" title="Freemasonry">Freemasonry</a> known as the Order of the Marguerite.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> References to their origins as versions of pre-existing external secret societies can be seen in a mural painted by Dunstan St Omer, depicting the holy trinity of <a href="/wiki/Osiris" title="Osiris">Osiris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horus" title="Horus">Horus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Isis" title="Isis">Isis</a>. </p>
      <p>The biggest festival of the year is the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia_Jazz_Festival" title="Saint Lucia Jazz Festival">Saint Lucia Jazz Festival</a>. Held in early May at multiple venues throughout the island, it draws visitors and musicians from around the world. The grand finale or main stage is held at the <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_Island_Island_National_Landmark_(Saint_Lucia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pigeon Island Island National Landmark (Saint Lucia)">Pigeon Island</a><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> which is located to the North of the Island. </p>
      <p>Traditionally in common with other Caribbean countries, Saint Lucia held a <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">carnival</a> before <a href="/wiki/Lent" title="Lent">Lent</a>. In 1999, the government moved Carnival to mid-July to avoid competing with the much larger <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_carnival" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinidad and Tobago carnival">Trinidad and Tobago carnival</a> and so as to attract more overseas visitors. </p>
      <p>In May 2009, Saint Lucians commemorated the 150th Anniversary of West Indian Heritage on the island. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Saint_Lucia" title="Sport in Saint Lucia">Sport in Saint Lucia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Beausejour_Stadium_Cricket_St_Lucia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Beausejour_Stadium_Cricket_St_Lucia.jpg/300px-Beausejour_Stadium_Cricket_St_Lucia.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Beausejour_Stadium_Cricket_St_Lucia.jpg/450px-Beausejour_Stadium_Cricket_St_Lucia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Beausejour_Stadium_Cricket_St_Lucia.jpg/600px-Beausejour_Stadium_Cricket_St_Lucia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Beausejour_Stadium_Cricket_St_Lucia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Daren_Sammy_Cricket_Ground" title="Daren Sammy Cricket Ground">Daren Sammy Cricket Ground</a> hosts international cricket matches for the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Darren_Sammy,_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Darren_Sammy%2C_2010.jpg/220px-Darren_Sammy%2C_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="286" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Darren_Sammy%2C_2010.jpg/330px-Darren_Sammy%2C_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Darren_Sammy%2C_2010.jpg/440px-Darren_Sammy%2C_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1446" data-file-height="1878"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Darren_Sammy,_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cricketer Daren Sammy.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands_cricket_team" title="Windward Islands cricket team">Windward Islands cricket team</a> includes players from Saint Lucia and plays in the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Four_Day_Competition" title="Regional Four Day Competition">West Indies regional tournament</a>. <a href="/wiki/Daren_Sammy" title="Daren Sammy">Daren Sammy</a> became the first Saint Lucian to represent the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies</a> on his debut in 2007, and since 2010 has captained the side.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> In an international career spanning 2003 to 2008, and including 41 ODIs and one Test, <a href="/wiki/Nadine_George" title="Nadine George">Nadine George</a> MBE became the first woman to score a Test century for the team.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Sammy and George were recognised by the Saint Lucian government as Sportsman of the Year and Sportswoman of the Year respectively for 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>For sailing enthusiasts, the annual <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Rally_for_Cruisers" title="Atlantic Rally for Cruisers">Atlantic Rally for Cruisers</a> (ARC) race begins in the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> and ends in Saint Lucia. The year 2015 marked the ARC's 30th year of existence. Every November, the race attracts over 200 boats and 1,200 people to sail across the Atlantic to the Caribbean. </p>
      <p>In 2019 a modern state of the art horse racing facility opened. One of the main contributors will be The China Horse Club, operators of race tracks in Asia. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Music and dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Music of Saint Lucia">Music of Saint Lucia</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">

        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Together with Caribbean music genres such as <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">Calypso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">Soca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dancehall" title="Dancehall">Dancehall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">Reggae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Compas" title="Compas">Compas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zouk_(musical_movement)" class="mw-redirect" title="Zouk (musical movement)">Zouk</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Salsa_music" title="Salsa music">Salsa</a>, Saint Lucia has a strong indigenous folk music tradition. Each May since 1991, Saint Lucia has hosted an internationally renowned <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia_Jazz_Festival" title="Saint Lucia Jazz Festival">Jazz Festival</a>. In 2013, the festival was re-branded The Saint Lucia Jazz &amp; Arts Festival which encompassed culture, visual art, alternative music, education, fashion, and food. </p>
      <p>Dancing in Saint Lucia is inspired by Caribbean culture and enjoys an active following. A popular folk dance is the <i><a href="/wiki/Kwadril" title="Kwadril">Kwadril</a></i>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Caribbean Cinemas operates in Saint Lucia. The cinema is located at Choc Estate in Castries. There is also a Bank of St. Lucia ATM, <a href="/wiki/Domino%27s_Pizza" title="Domino's Pizza">Domino's Pizza</a> outlet, &amp; a cafe [Rituals Coffee Shop] near the Cinema. </p>
      <p>Much of the scenery for the film <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dolittle_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dr. Dolittle (film)"><i>Dr. Dolittle</i></a> was shot in Saint Lucia in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Water_(1985_film)" title="Water (1985 film)"><i>Water</i></a> was shot on the island,<sup id="cite_ref-den_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-den-71">[71]</a></sup> as were parts of <a href="/wiki/Firepower_(film)" title="Firepower (film)"><i>Firepower</i></a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Saint_Lucia" title="Education in Saint Lucia">Education in Saint Lucia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Education Act provides for free and compulsory education in Saint Lucia from the ages of 5 to 15.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Public spending on education was at 5.8% among the 2002–2005 GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Saint Lucia has a community college (Sir Arthur Lewis Community College<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>), one university campus operated by the University of the West Indies Open Campus,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> and a few medical schools – <a href="/wiki/American_International_Medical_University" title="American International Medical University">American International Medical University</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_American_University_%E2%88%92_College_of_Medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="International American University − College of Medicine">International American University − College of Medicine</a>, Destiny University School of Medicine and Health Sciences, and the oldest of which is <a href="/wiki/Spartan_Health_Sciences_University" title="Spartan Health Sciences University">Spartan Health Sciences University</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Monroe_College" title="Monroe College">Monroe College</a>, a private for-profit college and graduate school based in New York City, established a campus in Saint Lucia in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucian_cuisine" title="Saint Lucian cuisine">Saint Lucian cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Saint Lucia's national dish is green figs and saltfish. </p>
      <p>The island's cuisine is a unique blend of West African<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, European (mainly British and French) and Indian cuisine; this creates dynamic meal dishes such as <a href="/wiki/Macaroni_pie" title="Macaroni pie">macaroni pie</a>, Stew chicken, <a href="/wiki/Rice_and_peas" title="Rice and peas">rice and peas</a>, fish broth or fish water, and <a href="/wiki/Soups" class="mw-redirect" title="Soups">soups</a> packed full with fresh locally produced vegetables. Typical essential foodstuffs are potatoes, onions, <a href="/wiki/Celery" title="Celery">celery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thyme" title="Thyme">thyme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coconut_milk" title="Coconut milk">coconut milk</a>, the very hot <a href="/wiki/Scotch_bonnet" title="Scotch bonnet">scotch bonnet peppers</a>, flour, and cornmeal. All mainstream meat and poultry are eaten in St. Lucia; meat and seafood are normally stewed and browned to create a rich gravy sometimes served over <a href="/wiki/Ground_provisions" title="Ground provisions">ground provisions</a> or rice. The island is also home to the famous fried dough, known by many as a bake or Johnny Cake. These bakes can be served with different sides, such as saltfish which is either sautéed or lightly fried along with red, green peppers, onions, and seasoned well. This is the most common way for bake to be prepared, though it can also be served with meats such as stewed chicken or beef. </p>
      <p>One popular Saint Lucian dessert is the pastry called a turnover. The pastry is made with sweetened coconut that is boiled with spices, some sugar, and whatever is satisfying. It is boiled until cooked to a light or dark brown colour; then the mixture is separated into various size portions placed on a rolled out piece of dough. The dough size may vary too depending on how much is desired, and lastly, it is baked in the oven until the colour of the turnover is nicely browned. </p>
      <p>Due to Saint Lucia's Indo-Caribbean population, curry is very popular; however due to the blend of cooking styles, curry dishes have a distinct Caribbean twist. Roti is typically served as a fast food meal: the bread itself is very flat (sometimes very thin) and is wrapped around curried vegetables such as chickpeas and potato, seafood such as shrimp and conch, or meats such as chicken, beef, goat, and liver. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBTQ_non-acceptance">LGBTQ non-acceptance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Lucia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: LGBTQ non-acceptance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Saint_Lucia" title="LGBT rights in Saint Lucia">Lesbian, gay, bisexual, and transgender (LGBT) people living in Saint Lucia</a> face legal challenges not experienced by non-LGBT members of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Saint Lucia prohibits male-on-male sexual activity, punishing those found guilty with 10 years in jail; the law is not enforced, however.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Saint Lucia was also the only UN member in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> to formally oppose the <a href="/wiki/UN_declaration_on_sexual_orientation_and_gender_identity" class="mw-redirect" title="UN declaration on sexual orientation and gender identity">UN declaration on sexual orientation and gender identity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> </p>
